    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer585372333794783733">In their first encounter, demigod Percy Jackson and magician Carter Kane had to battle a giant crocodile on Long Island.   <span id="freeText585372333794783733" style="display:none">In their first encounter, demigod Percy Jackson and magician Carter Kane had to battle a giant crocodile on Long Island. A month later, Annabeth Chase ran into Carter's sister, Sadie, on the A train to Rockaway, where the pair fought a god named Serapis. Now trouble is brewing again, this time on Governor's Island. An ancient Egyptian magician named Setne has come back from the dead and is experimenting with Egyptian and Greek magic, trying to become a god himself. He's so powerful and tricky that all four-Percy, Annabeth, Carter, and Sadie-have to team up against him. But their usual weapons and spells aren't going to cut it this time. Will the heroes be taken down by a wannabe god who looks like Elvis, or will they rise to the challenge?<br /><br />Told from Percy's point of view, this third demigod-magician crossover story has all of the spunk and action that Rick Riordan fans crave.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10387916288134814341"><b> To all the idiots who told me I won't hear anything from Percy again, you little fuckers. I have this super-duper-mega-awesome-book that tells me about another PERCY JACKSON adventure.<br/><br/>Don't try to come between me and my love again. I will rip you to pieces.</b></span>

  <span id="freeText16122014840633803106" style="display:none"><b>4 stars (Re-read 11/13/20) </b><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3621281959?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Son of Sobek: </a>★★★ ½<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3638537974?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Staff of Serapis:</a>★★★<br><br>The combination of Sadie and Percy's lack of braincells and Annabeth and Carter's overflowing brain power is perfection. I think this book was the best out of the three, but perhaps it's because it's the finale. And it's in Percy's POV! There is nothing better than that. The thing I noticed is that sometimes the dialogue is immature at times, which is weird, because even though I know it's directed towards an audience younger then mine, I have never felt that way reading PJO. I recently re-read that series this year, and I loved the light-hearted humor, but it felt juvenile here. Also again, I don't like Sadie, but she didn't have as big of presence considering it was split up with 4 people, so that was fine. I think the concept of this book is great, and I kind of want to re-read The Kane Chronichals now. Totally recommend to anyone that wants a fun and fast read!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1605248900i/30371088._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1138286529" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138286529" />
    <a title="Sanni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18712477-sanni"><img alt="Sanni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389007202p2/18712477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138286529?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sanni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sanni" href="/user/show/18712477-sanni">Sanni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138286529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16111108360230094949"><u>Before reading it:</u><br/><i>Told from Percy's point of view, this third demigod-magician crossover story has all of the spunk and action that Rick Riordan fans crave.</i><br/><br/><i>Told from Percy's point of view</i><br/><br/><i>PERCY'S POINT OF VIEW</i><br/><br/>I have been waiting for this moment for <b>so long</b>. I simply adore Percy's narrating voice and I have missed "hearing" it since The Last Olympian. I can't wait!<br/><br/><u>After reading it:</u><br/>Ah, Percy, I <i>had</i> missed hearing your voice in my head. The story was awesome, the Kanes were awesome, Annabeth was awe</span>
  <span id="freeText16111108360230094949" style="display:none"><u>Before reading it:</u><br /><i>Told from Percy's point of view, this third demigod-magician crossover story has all of the spunk and action that Rick Riordan fans crave.</i><br /><br /><i>Told from Percy's point of view</i><br /><br /><i>PERCY'S POINT OF VIEW</i><br /><br />I have been waiting for this moment for <b>so long</b>. I simply adore Percy's narrating voice and I have missed "hearing" it since The Last Olympian. I can't wait!<br /><br /><u>After reading it:</u><br />Ah, Percy, I <i>had</i> missed hearing your voice in my head. The story was awesome, the Kanes were awesome, Annabeth was awesome and Percy, naturally, was awesome too.<br /><blockquote>'He'll become immortal,' Annabeth guessed. 'A newly made god. Then he'll start vacuuming up all the Greek and Egyptian magic in the world.'<br />'Also he stole my sword,' I said. 'I want it back.'<br />The three of them stared at me.<br />'What?' I said. 'I like my sword.' </blockquote><br />Well at least someone has their priorities straight. Also, Crazy Elvis.</span>

<div id="review_1638674179" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638674179" />
    <a title="StMargarets" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49267198-stmargarets"><img alt="StMargarets" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452172151p2/49267198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638674179?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="StMargarets" class="user" itemprop="url" name="StMargarets" href="/user/show/49267198-stmargarets">StMargarets</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49267198-stmargarets?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49267198-stmargarets?shelf=children-s-literature">children-s-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638674179" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10103346728373328051">This is a short story - about 64 pages that brings together the main characters of Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson series with the brother and sister of the Kane Chronicle series. Percy and Annabeth are Greek demi-gods, while Sadie and Kane are Egyptian magicians. Normally you're not supposed to "cross the streams" in fantasy literature, but Riordan did, logically and cleverly. Seems Ptolemy was a historical figure that combined knowledge of the ancient Greeks and the Egyptians. So, Riordan just in</span>
  <span id="freeText10103346728373328051" style="display:none">This is a short story - about 64 pages that brings together the main characters of Rick Riordan's Percy Jackson series with the brother and sister of the Kane Chronicle series. Percy and Annabeth are Greek demi-gods, while Sadie and Kane are Egyptian magicians. Normally you're not supposed to "cross the streams" in fantasy literature, but Riordan did, logically and cleverly. Seems Ptolemy was a historical figure that combined knowledge of the ancient Greeks and the Egyptians. So, Riordan just invented a baddie that was going to follow in Ptolemy's footsteps, this time for evil and not for good. <br /><br />It's a fun premise and the best part is that the story is from Percy's first person point of view - something we haven't seen since the first Percy Jackson series that was completed in 2009. Percy is still my favorite of all of the many characters Riordan has created and it was great to hear from him again. Percy had the same view of the elaborate preparations and esoteric knowledge of the Egyptian magic that I did when I read the Kane Chronicles series, and it was fun to see him have to adapt. <br /><br />This is a story for hard-core fans who have read both series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10103346728373328051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1638674179">

  <span id="freeText13488791076798543251" style="display:none">The Crown of Ptolemy by Rick Riordan<br />Published 2015, Disney Hyperion<br />Stars: ★★★★☆ <br />Review also posted at: <a href="http://slapdashandsundry.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Slapdash &amp; Sundry</a><br /><br />I may have an unhealthy obsession with Rick Riordan. Seriously, I love Percy Jackson, I love Heroes of Olympus, I love the Kane Chronicles, and I'm waiting with bated breath for Magnus Chase and the Gods of Asgard to start this fall with Swords of Summer... so of course, I'm insta-buying anything with his name on it. <br /><br />This is the third in a series of crossovers between the characters from the two Greek/Roman series and the Kane siblings from the Kane Chronicles. <br /><br />The first starred Percy Jackson and Carter Kane, who had to fight a giant crocodile. <br /> <br />The second featured Annabeth Chase and Sadie Kane squaring off against a multi-headed monster. <br /><br />The Crown of Ptolemy features all four of them coming together to fight against the magician responsible for the, err, "issues" they faced in the first two. It includes lots of hijinks and of course, silly but hilarious dialogue.<br /><br />Join the fun, if you've read up to this point. Otherwise, jump back to the beginning and start with Percy Jackson and the Kane Chronicles. You won't regret it. They're loads of fun. :)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11475983065869028963">This review will be non-spoiler, I will post a spoiler review on my YouTube channel. I wanted to cry when I finished it. It was so perfect. This was the best way to say goodbye to Percy. The story is told from his first person POV and I loved walking through Percy's head again. I don't know about you, but his first person is much better than his third person. It it gives him back his humor and satisfied the craving to hear him, Annabeth, and the Kanes again.   <span id="freeText11475983065869028963" style="display:none">This review will be non-spoiler, I will post a spoiler review on my YouTube channel. I wanted to cry when I finished it. It was so perfect. This was the best way to say goodbye to Percy. The story is told from his first person POV and I loved walking through Percy's head again. I don't know about you, but his first person is much better than his third person. It it gives him back his humor and satisfied the craving to hear him, Annabeth, and the Kanes again. The loose ends on Percy's and the Kane's story lines where raped up nicely. This is the perfect way to say goodbye. Goodbye Percy, may you continue to inspire and change the lives of readers everywhere. </span>

<div id="review_1245603338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Pavitra (For The Love of Fictional Worlds)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20571769-pavitra-for-the-love-of-fictional-worlds"><img alt="Pavitra (For The Love of Fictional Worlds)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461136883p2/20571769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1245603338?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pavitra (For The Love of Fictional Worlds)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pavitra (For The Love of Fictional Worlds)" href="/user/show/20571769-pavitra-for-the-love-of-fictional-worlds">Pavitra (For The Love of Fictional Worlds)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20571769-pavitra-for-the-love-of-fictional-worlds?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1245603338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14690702507517385789"><b>Actual Rating 4.5 Stars </b> <br/><br/>For more reviews, do not forget to visit<a href='http://www.indianbookloveaffair.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>For The Love of Fictional Worlds</a> :) <br/><br/><b>
  <i> After all we'd been through, I was not going to let our lives end this way - devoured by a wannabe Elvis god with a pillbox hat.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Oh Percy! How I have missed you! <br/><br/>Best thing about this short story? (It is super short!) You are instantly transported to the world of Persassy and you wonder how have you even survived till now without it! *sighs* <br/><br/>This story is a continuation of both Son of Sobek a</span>
  <span id="freeText14690702507517385789" style="display:none"><b>Actual Rating 4.5 Stars </b> <br /><br />For more reviews, do not forget to visit<a href="http://www.indianbookloveaffair.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">For The Love of Fictional Worlds</a> :) <br /><br /><b>
  <i> After all we'd been through, I was not going to let our lives end this way - devoured by a wannabe Elvis god with a pillbox hat.</i>
</b><br /><br />Oh Percy! How I have missed you! <br /><br />Best thing about this short story? (It is super short!) You are instantly transported to the world of Persassy and you wonder how have you even survived till now without it! *sighs* <br /><br />This story is a continuation of both Son of Sobek and Staff of Serapis. Here both duos, Percabeth and Carter Kane and his sister Sadie Kane meet to defeat the Setne who is merging both the Egyptian and Greek to become a God! <br /><br />Honestly speaking I kinda sorta liked Setne. He had that cocky and sassiness that is usually missing from the different villains we have seen before. So yup, I did like him. He was adorable even with the taking over the world thing he had going on (Oh jeez, what does this say about my mental health, I don't even want to know!).<br /><br /><b>
  <i> Looking at Sadie, I could imagine that someday I'd have a little girl who looked like Annabeth and acted like me - a cute little hellion of a demigod, stomping through puddles and flattening monsters with magic camels."</i>
</b><br /><br />I don't want to write an extensive review for a short story, but ^^ this! This had me squealing and screaming like a crazed fangirl! Imagine! JUST IMAGINE ANNABETH AND PERCY'S LITTLE GIRL OR MAYBE A LITTLE BOY!!!!! EEEP!!! <br /><br />I really really hope that Uncle Rick writes some epilogue about them!! Because now that he has whet my appetite, I NEED TO KNOW EVERYTHING ABOUT THEIR PROGENY!!! UGGGHHHHHHH!!!<br /><br />The only thing that i didn't like (leaving the short length of the story aside!) is that there was no mention of the rest of the seven! Just a passing mention of the battle with Gaia. That's it! I would have thought that Uncle Rick, might have given a hint, a single hint if Leo made back home :( <br /><br />Because, do not lie, we all need that assurance! <br /><br />Beyond this, this book showed how absolutely mature Percy had gotten. And absolutely adorable Annabeth and Percy are together. And how now, I can't think of Sadie as anything but Percabeth's future daughter and Carter as their weirdy awesome relative. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"We had just passed our one - year dating anniversary. I figured I was a sort of ling - term investment for her. She hoped I would pay dividends eventually; if I died now, she would've put up with all my annoying qualities for nothing."</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14690702507517385789" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LiNUv57F5JEWrHZkVUKqWOCVC16BGC7kz1q2LahUYi+Tm6iDXcRjcHfxi12cdXfmpE5l76IXr4qhhTBDh1ZGfQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aqBfNu+5pnm1Z6pwW6+szLGAkySEpvTfRSB2NZKhN5rXGKMKLLghmNQ6V0mSmHFy9Vv9laepdbEr//BbvaMTyA==')})
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/42815482-the-crown-of-ptolemy">Quotes from The Crown of Ptolemy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;As for Sadie, she didn’t appear interested in strategy. She leaped from puddle to puddle in her combat boots. She hummed to herself, twirled like a little kid and occasionally pulled random things out of her backpack: wax animal figurines, some string, a piece of chalk, a bright yellow bag of candy.<br /><br />She reminded me of someone …<br /><br />Then it occurred to me. She looked like a younger version of Annabeth, but her fidgeting and hyperness reminded me of … well, me. If Annabeth and I ever had a daughter, she might be a lot like Sadie.<br /><br />Whoa.<br /><br />It’s not like I’d never dreamed about kids before. I mean, you date someone for over a year, the idea is going to be in the back of your mind somewhere, right? But still – I’m barely seventeen. I’m not ready to think too seriously about stuff like that. Also, I’m a demigod. On a day-to-day basis, I’m busy just trying to stay alive. <br /><br />Yet, looking at Sadie, I could imagine that someday maybe I’d have a little girl who looked like Annabeth and acted like me – a cute little hellion of a demigod, stomping through puddles and flattening monsters with magic camels.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;

          </div>
